  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_edcf70cd-d7bd-4748-956e-d16d78d66467'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7160969889398503248">Richard Lafargue is an eminent plastic surgeon haunted by dirty secrets. He has an operating theatre in the basement of his chateau and keeps his partner Eve imprisoned in her bedroom, a room he has equipped with an intercom and 300-watt speakers through which he bellows orders. Eve is only allowed out to be paraded at cocktail parties and on the last Sunday of each month,</span>
  <span id="freeText7160969889398503248" style="display:none">Richard Lafargue is an eminent plastic surgeon haunted by dirty secrets. He has an operating theatre in the basement of his chateau and keeps his partner Eve imprisoned in her bedroom, a room he has equipped with an intercom and 300-watt speakers through which he bellows orders. Eve is only allowed out to be paraded at cocktail parties and on the last Sunday of each month, when the couple visit a young woman in a mental asylum. Following these outings, Lafargue humiliates Eve by forcing her to perform lewd sexual acts with strangers while he watches through a one-way mirror. In alternating chapters, Jonquet introduces seemingly unrelated characters - a criminal on the run after murdering a policeman, and an abducted young man who finds himself chained naked in a dark chamber, forced to endure all manner of physical torture at the hands of a mysterious stranger, whom he calls 'Mygale', after a type of tropical spider. All of these characters are caught in a deceitful web, doomed to meet their fate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7160969889398503248" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script>  </div>

<div id="review_996287648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/996287648" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/996287648?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788498248951" href="/book/show/13539979-tar-ntula">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=drama">drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer996287648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10320935503985085105">I watched the film adaptation by Pedro Almodovar titled "The Skin I Live in" ("La Piel que Habito") in 2011. I liked a lot the movie and when I found out that it was based on a novel, I decided that eventually I will read it.<br/><br/>Finally it happened. First of all, taking out the major surprise in the storyline (don't worry, I won't spoil it), both stories are quite different, so it helped to appreciate the novel, while being the original story, and still have some surprises or unexpected developments</span>
  <span id="freeText10320935503985085105" style="display:none">I watched the film adaptation by Pedro Almodovar titled "The Skin I Live in" ("La Piel que Habito") in 2011. I liked a lot the movie and when I found out that it was based on a novel, I decided that eventually I will read it.<br /><br />Finally it happened. First of all, taking out the major surprise in the storyline (don't worry, I won't spoil it), both stories are quite different, so it helped to appreciate the novel, while being the original story, and still have some surprises or unexpected developments.<br /><br />However, I think that the film had the avantage of analyzing the strengths and weaknesses of the novel and being able to create an alternate storyline, in some ways milder and some ways stronger. <br /><br />I was hoping that the novel wouldn't have the limitations of the film in presenting the though and crude elements of the story that in both versions are kinda similar, however, while on the novel you met some more shocking scenes, at the end, I think that the overall impression of the development on the novel it falls in ending in a weak way from a strong premise with tremendous potential.<br /><br />Revenge and madness are primary factors in the novel to construct this twisted and bizarre story, however, I think that the character Dr. Richard Lafargue failed to acomplish my own expectations of fulfilling his plans of insane vengeance. Even more since the developments in a key sub-story put him in a priviledged position to extend his vendetta but he got like "cold feet" and remembering his own human nature and even developing some guilt merged with impossible "love" feelings. I mean, I think that if somebody took so heavy steps to engage a revenge that after all, it's quite justified, well, having second thoughts after being on it for years it's quite disappointing from the point of view of storytelling. Maybe, just maybe it's more realistic, I don't know, I am not psychologist to know if somebody can change so much and expressing feelings so impossible ones after being for several years in the process of such deranged retribution.<br /><br />But even the other main character is quite contradictional, maybe a little more justified for experiencing such unique events, however even so, it's also kinda dissapointing.<br /><br />The story had so much potential for ending in a perfect scary tale, but I don't know if the author got frighten himself for the novel that he was writing. I wouldn't blame him since it's indeed a twisted and sick story. However, if he conceptualized it and decided to publish it, well, I think that he should have the nerves to finish on its full potential.<br /><br />And after reading the novel, I didn't get the impression that he did that. It was like running a marathon and tripping over just a few meters from the finishing line and while he crossed it, he did it on limping without the same impact that he started the race.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10320935503985085105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762493905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10555028829774579574"><b>**5 "CONUNDRUM OF CONFUSION” STARS*** </b><br/><br/> I started this book w/ minimal expectations and in return they were met 10 fold. TARANTULA is <u>MOST DEFINITELY <b> NOT </b>FOR EVERYONE </u>…. This tale will test the readers patients, endurance, frustration level and fundamental math skills **1+1= ? .. WHAT?**...... Here's a little glimpse of emotions you can expect to endure....<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384802643ra/6971622.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429740ra/861102.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386120ra/745383.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/414916.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384753005ra/6955505.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384753005ra/6955504.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384641157ra/6922877.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>..okay, you’ve been warned. </b><br/><br/>The chaos begins with the Dapper<b> Richard Lafargue</b> summoning<b> Eve</b> in this manner--> <i>"For God sakes, hurry up you </i></span>
  <span id="freeText10555028829774579574" style="display:none"><b>**5 "CONUNDRUM OF CONFUSION” STARS*** </b><br><br> I started this book w/ minimal expectations and in return they were met 10 fold. TARANTULA is <u>MOST DEFINITELY <b> NOT </b>FOR EVERYONE </u>…. This tale will test the readers patients, endurance, frustration level and fundamental math skills **1+1= ? .. WHAT?**...... Here's a little glimpse of emotions you can expect to endure....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384802643ra/6971622.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380429740ra/861102.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386120ra/745383.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/414916.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384753005ra/6955505.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384753005ra/6955504.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384641157ra/6922877.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>..okay, you’ve been warned. </b><br><br>The chaos begins with the Dapper<b> Richard Lafargue</b> summoning<b> Eve</b> in this manner--&gt; <i>"For God sakes, hurry up you piece of shit!"</i>. Richard is a highly regarded plastic surgeon whom has some rather disturbing secrets. Eve is his girlfriend? Wife ? Whore ? Prisoner? Expensive play toy? All of the above? None of the above???... <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384803428i/6973300.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Vincent</b> and<b> Alex</b> confused me the most. I couldn't understand their purpose but their actually the characters whom matter the most... or maybe they mean absolutely nothing at all. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384803965ra/6973840.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Viviene</b> is <b> Mygale</b> &lt;--- who? *EXACTLY* daughter who's gone mad.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/497617.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And...unfortunately that is all I can say without giving away all the shebang.... This is a story where REVENGE is a dish that's best served <b>BOLD!!!</b><br><br>Now...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384804787i/6973981.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>.... be prepared to have your mind blown.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384734737ra/6947606.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Thank you Enigma for recommending such an unforgettable story...MUAH! </i><br><br><b> For more reviews, Free E-books and Giveaways<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407612151i/10746470._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></b></span>

<div id="review_648801912" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648801912" />
    <a title="Kynthos-the-Archer (Kyn)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn"><img alt="Kynthos-the-Archer (Kyn)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511264057p2/9739117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648801912?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kynthos-the-Archer (Kyn)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kynthos-the-Archer (Kyn)" href="/user/show/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn">Kynthos-the-Archer (Kyn)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846687945" href="/book/show/11367816-tarantula">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who could appreciate a good disturbing mind fuqking - crime and psychological thriller genre.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=thriller_suspenseful_cliffhanging">thriller_suspenseful_cliffhanging</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=dark-fics-or-story">dark-fics-or-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=in-library">in-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=injury_bodily-harm">injury_bodily-harm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=thoughts-provoking">thoughts-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=weak-defenseless-protagonist">weak-defenseless-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=collaring_on-leash">collaring_on-leash</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=submissive-protagonist">submissive-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9739117-kynthos-the-archer-kyn?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648801912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4234891554959699365"><br/><br/><b>Please try to <u>refrain</u> from looking at my shelf tags for this book. Unless of course you don't mind spoiling this book before you could get to it. You have been adequately warned.</b> <br/><br/><br/>Rating: <b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>What a twisted book with a twisted ending to match. I was left aghast and reeling with mixed emotion after finishing it. <br/><br/>Be ready for a dark and twisted story driven by hate and fear. It all started with a crime of lust and selfish indulgence which lead to the destruction of an innocent young girl. But </span>
  <span id="freeText4234891554959699365" style="display:none"><br><br><b>Please try to <u>refrain</u> from looking at my shelf tags for this book. Unless of course you don't mind spoiling this book before you could get to it. You have been adequately warned.</b> <br><br><br>Rating: <b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>What a twisted book with a twisted ending to match. I was left aghast and reeling with mixed emotion after finishing it. <br><br>Be ready for a dark and twisted story driven by hate and fear. It all started with a crime of lust and selfish indulgence which lead to the destruction of an innocent young girl. But was that enough reason to seek justice in the most vile manner? And how far should it go before it's too much that it destroys you too?<br><br>The story was set in France and centers around Richard Lafargue a prominent plastic surgeon and his disturbing relationship with a beautiful mysterious young woman named Eve, whom Lafargue had under lock and key literally. She would only be released from her gilded cage whenever Lafargue felt like parading her around his high society social circle. <br><br>Although Lafargue seems to dote on her at times, buying her gifts and taking her out to lavish dinning, he would also subject her to perform unspeakable sexual acts with multiple partners just to debase her and enjoy her sufferings. On the surface it looks like Eve was nothing more than a pet or a toy to Lafargue but the reasons behind it was far more devious than it appears to be. <br><br>Lafargue is quite a manipulative and malicious character. Highly intelligent and dangerously cunning. The mental tortures he subjected Eve to was both ingenious and effective in molding her body and soul to his will. It was chilling to see him in action sometimes. He kept me wondering what was truly on his mind? Has he gone mad as Eve perceived him to be or is his hatred really that all consuming? How far could one go driven by hatred? When will it be enough to quench his thirst for justification? <br><br>I could understand Eve's confused state of mind whenever it comes to Lafargue as he was never truly constant especially in the beginning of their relationship. He would hurt her at one time and dotes on her the next. When Eve tries to lean on his tenderness, she would be promptly slapped away only to be comforted again when she slips into depression. <br><br>In my humble opinion, the writing was beautiful and refine albeit chilling and disturbing at the same time. I shudder often thinking of all those irreversible physical and psychological scarring on the victim. To be so forcefully changed forever. How could one forgave another for causing such grievous harm on them for whatever justification at all?<br><br>I am in total agreement with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/540460249" rel="nofollow noopener">Mizuki Genshou's review</a> that this is a tale of suffering of the body and soul, domination and submission, hurt and comfort, love and hate. An intriguing twisted relationship between predator and prey, prisoner and jailer. <br><br>I especially like this remark by Mizuki on her review, <b>
  <i>"I found it to be very bold and imaginative, even kind of sexy in a twisted way."</i>
</b> I ditto that wholeheartedly although I am too not sure I would or should be tagging this book under my BDSM shelf. <br><br>I have already mentioned right at the beginning of this review that the ending has taken me by surprise and left me amazed in a shocked way as it wasn't what I have expected to happen at all. A thousand questions flooded my mind at once. How I wish I could discuss it with someone, anyone, just to get it off my chest. What motivates her decision towards the end? Why? I have a few speculations myself. Ahh... how I love it when a book does that to me, making me think and delve deeper into the story even after it ends. I would love to encounter other books of similar nature. This one was such a rare gem. <br><br>Both the book and the movie adaptation was unique in itself and are equally good. Each has its own set of storyline with the movie preserving only part of the premise of this story. What I love in the movie was not found in the book and vice versa. If you still have to know which I prefer best, I'll go with the book because it is inevitably more detailed in nature.<br><br>This story isn't going to leave my mind anytime soon as it has etched itself deep into my psyche. It was such a page turner for me that I have finished it in a day! As a slow reader, this is a record for me.<br><br><br><b>This book should thrill most <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/75751-depraved-minds-club-dmc" rel="nofollow noopener">DMCers</a>.</b><br><br>To those who must know if this book contains a HEA/HFN, click here - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I would say, it's a rather warped HFN with possibility of a twisted romance as I do not feel the effect of Stockholm Syndrome here. Unless, it's an act of redemption that spur that unexpected choice at the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><b> (Only click if you MUST really know before you could even consider reading this book. So please don't blame me if you spoil it for yourself. Hehe)</b><br><br><br><br><u>Extra Info:</u><br><br>Translated from French by Donald Nicholson-Smith<br>Original Title: Mygale (<i>Tarantula</i>, was adopted for English translation)<br>Approximate Word Count: 35,000 words<br><br>Title of the film adaptation: <b><a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1189073/%20" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>The Skin I Live In (2011) / "La piel que habito" (French title)</b> (Directed by Pedro Almodóvar)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794537i/593914._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794537i/593915._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4234891554959699365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Xandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6600821-xandra"><img alt="Xandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587055091p2/6600821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266815079?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Xandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Xandra" href="/user/show/6600821-xandra">Xandra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=thriller-mystery-crime-horror">thriller-mystery-crime-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=gender">gender</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=french">french</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=european">european</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=by-men">by-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=transgressive">transgressive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6600821-xandra?shelf=1950-1999">1950-1999</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266815079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14022171841952867453">Maybe you have to be a sick and deranged individual to enjoy this. Or maybe you need to be able to detach yourself a little from your own humanity and perceive human nature with a neutral eye. One thing is clear: <i>Tarantula</i> is not for the faint of heart.<br/><br/>For me, this is hands down <b>the best revenge book I’ve ever read!</b> I seriously can’t imagine a more terrifying form of revenge than the one presented here (and I assure you, I have a wild imagination). Complex type of vengeance too, if you think abo</span>
  <span id="freeText14022171841952867453" style="display:none">Maybe you have to be a sick and deranged individual to enjoy this. Or maybe you need to be able to detach yourself a little from your own humanity and perceive human nature with a neutral eye. One thing is clear: <i>Tarantula</i> is not for the faint of heart.<br /><br />For me, this is hands down <b>the best revenge book I’ve ever read!</b> I seriously can’t imagine a more terrifying form of revenge than the one presented here (and I assure you, I have a wild imagination). Complex type of vengeance too, if you think about it, both physically and psychologically scarring. Not to mention irreversible. <br /><br />You’ll shudder often. You’ll probably guess some of the twists and turns, but you’ll refuse to believe you might be right. Your feelings will be toyed with ruthlessly and the ending will leave you gaping. And you’ll never get bored. <br /><br />The writing has a chilling simplicity and, without being the best I’ve encountered, it’s fitting.<br /><br />Highly disturbing and scary without being gory, <i>Mygale</i> (or <i>Tarantula</i> as it was translated) and Almodovar’s loose adaptation <i>“The Skin I Live In”</i> are both brilliant in their own way. The movie keeps, of course, the big horrifying twist, but you’ll be amazed to realize how the essential changes Almodovar makes create <b>a whole new story</b>. Highly recommended!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14022171841952867453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_770197896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770197896" />
    <a title="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6294320-carol-starangel-s-reviews-allen"><img alt="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386893634p2/6294320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/770197896?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen" href="/user/show/6294320-carol-starangel-s-reviews-allen">Carol (StarAngel&#39;s Reviews) Allen</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14840371187895151575"><b>*****5 Puzzling Stars*****</b><br/><br/>I am not sure how to begin, I can just tell you as I read this I felt like I was solving a puzzle.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398039103ra/9360181.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Not a very easy to solve puzzle, at least for this girl, might I add. Dr. Lafargue keeps a woman, Eve, confined in his home. Eve is only permitted to leave the home for dinners, social obligations, oh and...when</span>
  <span id="freeText14840371187895151575" style="display:none"><b>*****5 Puzzling Stars*****</b><br><br>I am not sure how to begin, I can just tell you as I read this I felt like I was solving a puzzle.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398039103ra/9360181.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Not a very easy to solve puzzle, at least for this girl, might I add. While I was reading it I had a million different possibilities as to what could possibly be going on. <br><br>The story is about Dr. Lafargue, an eccentric plastic surgeon. Dr. Lafargue keeps a woman, Eve, confined in his home. Eve is only permitted to leave the home for dinners, social obligations, oh and...when he is prostituting her out. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397693596ra/9313242.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yeah, I had my "What??" face on a lot while reading this.<br><br>The whole situation with Dr. Lafargue and Eve, is odd because Eve accepts her situation with Dr. Lafargue and is pleasant when taken out, and even helps find "customers" for herself...<b>SAY WHAT!!</b><br><br>We also meet Viviane. Dr. Lafargue and Eve visit her in a psych ward...<b>UM, WHY??</b><br><br>Then there is Alex and Vincent, who I felt like were not even necessary characters in the beginning...<b>YOUR WAY OFF!!</b><br><br>I know this review is vague, but there is only so much that can be said without giving away the plot twists. <br><br>I will say this book had me thinking nonstop, and when it all came to together I was still like <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/563952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>In my opinion this story had a happy ending. I finished this hours ago and I am still contemplating about it. That is why I give it 5 Stars.<br><br><b>With that let me add, this isn't for everyone. I would have probably quit if I wasn't so hell bent on figuring this story out, and I had not had encouragement from my GR Friends. This book had me questioning my intelligence and I had a million different "theories".</b><br><br>But, to sum everything up...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389134751ra/7993715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Thanks to Wonderful Jahy for recommending!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14840371187895151575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=chinese-translation">chinese-translation</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer540460249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2871484964254300555">Take my words, This book is fascinating. <br/><br/>The story is a brilliant but bizarre mixture of thriller and erotica, a complicative, finely crafted tale of revenge and suffering, domination and submission, (both mental and physical) abuse and tenderness, love and hate. It shows us a heart-stoppingly violent power struggle between two 'men' and two 'women', it revealed the complicated relationship between predator and prey, prisoner and jailer.<br/><br/>It's difficult to comment on Mygale without spoiling the su</span>
  <span id="freeText2871484964254300555" style="display:none">Take my words, This book is fascinating. <br /><br />The story is a brilliant but bizarre mixture of thriller and erotica, a complicative, finely crafted tale of revenge and suffering, domination and submission, (both mental and physical) abuse and tenderness, love and hate. It shows us a heart-stoppingly violent power struggle between two 'men' and two 'women', it revealed the complicated relationship between predator and prey, prisoner and jailer.<br /><br />It's difficult to comment on Mygale without spoiling the surprise. So I'll leave it to you to discover what's in store for you. Even before I read Mygale, I knew that director Pedro Almodovar had adapted it into a movie called 'The Skin I Live In' (but the author of Mygale, Mr Jonquet passed away before he could see the movie). Now I'm definitely looking forward to watch the movie as well.<br /><br />In the recommendation and also in one of the reviews for Mygale, the reviewer went into great length to talk about Marquis de Sade, von Sacher-Masoch; also helpfully informed us the difference between realistic, practical BDSM lifestyle and fantasy, but I found what makes Mygale so successful and unsettling is that the novel blurs the lines between 'sane', 'acceptable' BDSM practice and the 'bad', 'insane' and illegal fantasy of imprisoning someone and changing him or her according to one's liking. I found it to be very bold and imaginative, even kind of sexy in a twisted way. <br /><br />I'm also impressed by the author for creating plot twists which seem to be bizarre and outlandish but still managed to keep the plots make sense. Bravo, Mr. Jonquet. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14447989135468345124">I love my dark reads, I love them clever, to leave me guessing and at the end to be completely blown away by elements I didn't forsee coming. Tarantula does that and more, what a clever short novel that packed a big punch, full of twists and turns. It sure left an big impact, the writing was skillful and engaging.<br/><br/>The main plot narrates the story of expert plastic surgeon, Richard Lafargue, a mysterious character who keeps a woman, Eve, captive in his home. Richard uses Eve to perform for him wit</span>
  <span id="freeText14447989135468345124" style="display:none">I love my dark reads, I love them clever, to leave me guessing and at the end to be completely blown away by elements I didn't forsee coming. Tarantula does that and more, what a clever short novel that packed a big punch, full of twists and turns. It sure left an big impact, the writing was skillful and engaging.<br><br>The main plot narrates the story of expert plastic surgeon, Richard Lafargue, a mysterious character who keeps a woman, Eve, captive in his home. Richard uses Eve to perform for him with other men the lewdest acts and sometimes violent ones are committed against her, while he watches from a one way mirror. Lafargue keeps Eve locked up and seemingly is only satisfied when he sees her broken. It's revealed later on that he also has a daughter in a psychiatric hospital, whom he visits regularly; with each visit, his pain at seeing her so unwell increases. Another subplot is of a thief and a murderer, whose path crosses later with Richard's and Eve's. Here's where I will stop talking about the plot. <br><br>I did guess one twist earlier on in the story, which added to my questions, What purpose does it serve. I kept reading, waiting for the end reveal and turning the pages to reach the big climax.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1412886334ra/11436919.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br> <i>
  <b>‘His suffering had to be appeased, and Eve existed solely for this purpose.’</b>
</i><br><br><br>Well this book was totally unexpected, original and very cleverly narrated. I loved the ending and for that I may seek professional help, I actually had an 'awww' moment, the ending while unexpected, shouldn't inspire an 'awww' moment. Don't worry, Jahy, I'll send you the number when I find a good doctor.<br><br>I'm planning now to see the movie, glad I resisted doing so before reading this. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6736891882643019782">This novel was uncomfortable, strange and somewhat disturbing. It's about a man who keeps a young woman hostage. That's all you're going</span>
  <span id="freeText6736891882643019782" style="display:none">This novel was uncomfortable, strange and somewhat disturbing. Unlike anything I've read before, I really enjoyed it and it kept me guessing, even when I had a feeling of what was going on, I wasn't sure if that was what was actually happening or just my imagination at play. It is also incredibly well written I thought.<br /><br />This is one of those stories where you can't say much or you'll give too much away, so I will try not to. It's about a man who keeps a young woman hostage. That's all you're going to get. Prepare to have your expectations surpassed as this is nothing like you've ever read.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book if you like disturbing, 'wtf?' kind of reads.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6736891882643019782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12070118301778891276" style="display:none">A great 'making you pay' story that reminds me of Franju's "Eyes Without a Face." It has that slightly surreal horror aspect to it. And many years later I am in Paris and looking for something to read in English, I found Joquet's "Tarantula." I purchased it and once I got on the plane i realized it was the British edition of "Mygale." So that was a disappointing moment. But alas I re-read the book.<br /><br />Its a masterpiece! As I mentioned it does have that Franju horror aspect, but it is also a very nasty revenge story. Almost on the surreal level of violence and behavior. I have read that Pedro Amodovar is doing a film on this - and I can him doing it campy. But alas it is truly a horror story. A great noir horror thriller.</span>

  <span id="freeText4778596343172870041" style="display:none"><br /><br /> What a beautiful monstrosity of a book! I loved it, every twisted part of it. The story centres on famed plastic surgeon Richard Lafargue who has many secrets (ones you can't even begin to imagine to know) and Eve, his partner, who he keeps looked away in her room and forces her to do unspeakable things. Obviously it's an intriguing plot however nothing can really prepare you for Lafargue's reasoning behind his actions and the final outcome. Written by Thierry Jonquet, this makes for a must read although much too short. I have tried looking for other of Jonquet's books that have been translated into English and unfortunately 'Tarantula' was the only one I could find. Recommended read however not for the light hearted... </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer768089521" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17261800005439606765">I saw Pedro Almodóvar’s film The Skin I live In before discovering this novel and was blown away by it. Reading this has blown me away once again and will remain in my memory for quite some time. This book (packed into just over 100 pages) has left me emotionally reeling, which doesn’t happen often enough.<br/><br/>This has been mentioned in previous reviews here that the film and novel (although the main plot remains) will be a totally different experience and advise all to do both. <br/>I’m glad that I could</span>
  <span id="freeText17261800005439606765" style="display:none">I saw Pedro Almodóvar’s film The Skin I live In before discovering this novel and was blown away by it. Reading this has blown me away once again and will remain in my memory for quite some time. This book (packed into just over 100 pages) has left me emotionally reeling, which doesn’t happen often enough.<br /><br />This has been mentioned in previous reviews here that the film and novel (although the main plot remains) will be a totally different experience and advise all to do both. <br />I’m glad that I could still remain shocked and horrified by this twisted story rather than moan to my friends about how the film adaptation missed out so much. I do wish I had discovered the book first though. <br /><br />You won’t find a multitude of fancy metaphors in this story either. It’s not needed.<br /><br />This is not for the faint of heart. I am sat here still confused over whom my sympathy should lie with, and questioning why I should even be contemplating sympathising with any character other than <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the original victim, Viviane Lafargue!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I will be amazed if I ever come across another revenge story that goes to such extremes.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_336236453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/336236453" />
    <a title="Joel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9764083-joel"><img alt="Joel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581686544p2/9764083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/336236453?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joel" href="/user/show/9764083-joel">Joel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback with flaps 9788376489056" href="/book/show/12638165-tarantula">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336236453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10953790355393333075">Clocking in at around 120pp., Jonquet’s Mygale is a fast read indeed with a few twists and turns, one which in particular is a bit incongruous with what has happened before but which the movie totally ignored.<br/> <br/><br/>There were two main characters in the novel: Richard Lafargue, a renowned plastic surgeon, and Eve, who may or may not be his girlfriend. Lafarque has a weird penchant for humiliating Even when it suits him. He finds Johns for her and he watches from a distance and vicariously lives off th</span>
  <span id="freeText10953790355393333075" style="display:none">Clocking in at around 120pp., Jonquet’s Mygale is a fast read indeed with a few twists and turns, one which in particular is a bit incongruous with what has happened before but which the movie totally ignored.<br /> <br /><br />There were two main characters in the novel: Richard Lafargue, a renowned plastic surgeon, and Eve, who may or may not be his girlfriend. Lafarque has a weird penchant for humiliating Even when it suits him. He finds Johns for her and he watches from a distance and vicariously lives off this humiliation. What set this off? Without being spoilerrific, this has something to do with the grand scheme and the ending.<br /><br />When Almodovar filmed this movie, I had concluded that this thriller would have a gender bending element for which the director has been known for (Bad Education springs to mind). I just didn’t have the inkling that that gender bending element was too far out but, in more ways than one, very cruel indeed.<br /><br />Last time I read a French thriller, Sebastien Japrisot’s the Lady in the Car with the Glasses and a Gun had a dreamlike quality which this book didn’t have. On the one hand, Mygale had the stuff of nightmares which most men wouldn’t even dream of.<br /><br />After ruminating over the facts of the books, the tales that it has spun, I would have opined that Alex Barny, and whatever his story is could have been dropped. Eve’s backstory could have been enough. Almodovar was able to purse together events which made Lafarque’s daughter, Viviane, insane. In any case, I found that more unnerving than what has been detailed in the book. This event which catapulted Lafarque’s cruelty into centerstage may be plausible enough.<br /><br />This book shares a few things in common with Tim Krabbe’s Vanishing. However, the main antagonist in Vanishing had evil in spades, and in the end remained unrepentant which didn’t find its way in Mygale (redemption factor sometimes can be such a bummer).</span>
  <a data-text-id="10953790355393333075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2619823016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4872743226475272207">Years ago, I watched the movie "The Skin I live in" which is based on this book and I loved it so much that I immediately bought the eBook which has been in Kindle library ever since. Now I finally picked it up and I couldn’t put it down.<br/><br/>First of all: If you haven’t seen the movie, please do yourself a favour and read the book first! There’s a big reveal in the end and you will like the book SO much more if you don’t know about it.<br/><br/>You also should be aware that neither the book nor the movie is f</span>
  <span id="freeText4872743226475272207" style="display:none">Years ago, I watched the movie "The Skin I live in" which is based on this book and I loved it so much that I immediately bought the eBook which has been in Kindle library ever since. Now I finally picked it up and I couldn’t put it down.<br /><br />First of all: If you haven’t seen the movie, please do yourself a favour and read the book first! There’s a big reveal in the end and you will like the book SO much more if you don’t know about it.<br /><br />You also should be aware that neither the book nor the movie is for everyone. All the characters are pretty messed up and I really mean all of them. There’s no one you can really sympathise with. There’s also a lot of sexual, physical and mental violence.<br /><br />For those who are not discouraged yet: The book is totally worth your time. For me it’s a good thing that it’s not longer than 128 pages, it’s the perfect lengths, to try to make the story longer for the sake of more pages would have harmed the flow. I can imagine that the beginning is very confusing and a bit tedious if you don’t know where it goes. Just stick with it, it will all make sense. The outcome is still messed up, but it will make sense.<br /><br />Jonquet’s writing is really good but not great. This, however, could be a problem with the translation as the book was originally published in French. I read the English version.<br /><br />It’s a dark and twisted book with a surprising end and personally I really enjoyed it despite the fact that I knew where it was going. I just wish I had read the book first! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4872743226475272207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DY13vfnkee7Jn3J+czi9L2p1RsEceFiFDT/qfSjRxCSayEMa7qe+Zp812J2lzAvDW+9IQi8tCeFq1VO8rlRgQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('srmkWhek3SX/vcb874wA3Iig6bMF5Dh6pFrIYOPIvj8l/JD9AOcarakXbB85eLYwuTrnMDaxaR7DsHGhZU0aWA==')})
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_180026'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/180026.Diary_of_a_Lost_Girl?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Diary of a Lost Girl: The Autobiography of Kola Boof<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/33118.Kola_Boof?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Kola Boof<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.11 avg rating &mdash; 706 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2003\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer14064462568138088647\">Kola Boof\'s long awaited autobiography \"Diary of a Lost Girl\" is nothing less than magnificent. Many will be spellbound by more than 90 pages detailing her terrifying experience as Osama Bin Laden\'s former mistress, but the Sudanese-born Novelist/Poe<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText14064462568138088647\" style=\"display:none\">Kola Boof\'s long awaited autobiography &quot;Diary of a Lost Girl&quot; is nothing less than magnificent. Many will be spellbound by more than 90 pages detailing her terrifying experience as Osama Bin Laden\'s former mistress, but the Sudanese-born Novelist/Poet writes even more profoundly about the hardships of being vaginally circumcised, about witnessing her birth parents killed in her presence as a small child, about slavery and Arabism in Sudan, about being adopted and raised in the U.S. by African Americans, about her quest for true love, and in one particularly daring chapter, about her hopes for the future of her sons. Thomson\'s latest finds three very different characters--an aimless waitress, a reluctant hit man, and an ambitious young marketing executive--linked by the sudden success of a new soft drink. And James Lyle, the striving marketer who thought up the brainwashing scheme in the first place, is deliberately out of the loop about its consequences. To the reader of 1922 it presented a shocking look at a little known phenomenon. Today, while we are more familiar with drugs because of their widespread use in our culture, Diary of a Drug Fiend remains one o fthe most intense, detailed and accurate accounts of drug addiction and the drug experience.\n\nThe book was written by Crowley after years of deep personal study and experimentation with drugs. It is the story of a young man and woman who fall madly in love and whirl through Europe in a frenzied haze of heroin/cocaine adventure. Their ecstacy is brought to an abrupt end when their drug supply is cut off and despair replaces joy. Through the guidance of King Lamus, a master Adept, they free themselves from the entanglements of addition by the application of practical Magick.\n\nThe narrative carries the reader aloft through the brilliance of the imagery created by this master of language; his prose development parallels the growth and increasing depth of his characters in an uncanny fashion. This is a book to be read and reread. It will also prove a useful document to doctors, lawyers, police and addicts for its unique and precise presentation of the psychology of addiction and the possibility of its cure through the <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6340807485347932094">Thierry Jonquet was a French writer who specialised in crime novels with political themes. he was born in Paris; his most recent and best known novel outside of France was <i>Mygale</i> (2003), which was published in English translation as <i>Tarantula</i> in 2005 (Serpent's Tail). He wrote over 20 novels in French, including <i>Le bal des débris, Moloch</i> and <i>Rouge c'est la vie</i>.<br/><br/>Jonquet died aged 55 in hospital in P</span>
  <span id="freeText6340807485347932094" style="display:none">Thierry Jonquet was a French writer who specialised in crime novels with political themes. he was born in Paris; his most recent and best known novel outside of France was <i>Mygale</i> (2003), which was published in English translation as <i>Tarantula</i> in 2005 (Serpent's Tail). He wrote over 20 novels in French, including <i>Le bal des débris, Moloch</i> and <i>Rouge c'est la vie</i>.<br /><br />Jonquet died aged 55 in hospital in Paris.<br /><br /><i>Tarantula</i> has been adapted for the cinema by acclaimed Spanish director Pedro Almodóvar.<br /></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/903717-mygale">Quotes from Mygale</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Dans ta tête, tu avais donné un nom au maître. Tu n’osais l’employer en sa présence, bien entendu. Tu l’appelais «Mygale», en souvenir de tes terreurs passées. Mygale, un nom à consonance féminine, un nom d’animal répugnant qui ne cadrait pas à son sexe ni au raffinement extrême qu’il savait montrer dans le choix de tes cadeaux…<br />Mais Mygale car il était telle l’araignée, lente et secrète, cruelle et féroce, avide et insaisissable dans ses desseins, caché quelque part dans cette demeure où il te séquestrait depuis des mois, une toile de luxe, un piège doré dont il était le geôlier et toi le détenu.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/595032-dans-ta-t-te-tu-avais-donn-un-nom-au-ma-tre">106 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Tu n’étais plus qu’un insecte prisonnier d’une araignée repue, qui te gardait en réserve pour un repas à venir. Elle t’avait capturé pour te savourer en toute quiétude, quand l’envie lui viendrait de goûter ton sang. Tu imaginais ses pattes velues, ses gros yeux globuleux, implacables, son ventre mou, gorgé de viande, vibrant, gélatineux, et ses crocs venimeux, sa bouche noire qui allait te sucer la vie.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/595030-tu-n-tais-plus-qu-un-insecte-prisonnier-d-une-araign-e-repue-qui">104 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
